## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration ODE models)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a species concentration A, which is the standard object modeled in chemical kinetics via rate laws. With only (t, A) available, the most likely structures are single-species batch/reactor kinetics: order-based consumption/production terms in A, possible equilibrium offsets, and explicit time-dependent forcing or time-varying rate constants.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zeroth-order kinetics (constant-rate consumption/production): dA_dt = -c0 (surface-limited or saturated regime approximated as constant rate)
- First-order decay/formation: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, dilution, radioactive-analogy kinetics)
- Second-order decay (bimolecular with identical reactants or pseudo-second-order): dA_dt = -c0 * A**2
- n-th order power-law rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical overall reaction order / fractal-like kinetics)
- Shifted power-law (background/offset concentration scale): dA_dt = -c0 * (A + c1)**c2 (effective order with baseline or regularization near A≈0)
- Reversible first-order to an equilibrium level: dA_dt = -c0 * (A - c1) (relaxation toward A_eq = c1)
- Linear sink + constant source (CSTR/batch with feed or constant generation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1
- Autocatalytic / self-accelerating then self-limiting form: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (mass-action autocatalysis with finite capacity/limiting reagent lumped)
- General quadratic mass-action surrogate: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (lumped reversible + autocatalytic contributions)
- Inhibition-like rational rate (complexation or self-inhibition): dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate reduced at higher A by inhibitory complex formation)
- Time-varying first-order rate constant (slow drift in conditions): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * t) * A (k(t) approximately linear in time)
- Exponentially relaxing rate constant (transient heating/cooling or catalyst activation): dA_dt = -(c0 + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)) * A
- Catalyst deactivation / activity loss multiplier: dA_dt = -c0 * A * exp(-c1 * t) (effective rate decreases as activity decays)
- Periodic forcing (pulsed illumination/feeding/mixing): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * sin(c2 * t) (external periodic source term)
- Transient source term superposed on decay (impulse-like feed or initiation): dA_dt = -c0 * A + c1 * exp(-c2 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Consumption vs production: a dominant negative proportionality to A (e.g., -c0*A) indicates net consumption; sign flips or additive positive terms indicate net generation or inflow.
- Reaction order fingerprint: dependence like A, A**2, or A**c1 maps to unimolecular/bimolecular/overall empirical orders (mass-action-lumped kinetics).
- Approach to equilibrium: structures of the form -c0*(A - c1) imply relaxation toward a steady concentration A_eq = c1 (reversible or buffered system).
- Autocatalysis signature: presence of A*(c - A) (or a positive A term plus negative A**2 term) indicates self-acceleration at low A and self-limitation at higher A.
- Reactor/source effects: an additive constant (+c1) alongside a linear sink (-c0*A) is consistent with continuous generation/inflow balancing first-order removal.
- Condition drift: explicit t in a rate coefficient multiplying A, e.g., -(c0 + c1*t)*A, suggests changing temperature, mixing, light intensity, or catalyst state over time.
- Catalyst/activity decay: multiplicative exp(-c*t) on the kinetic term indicates decaying catalytic activity or availability of reactive intermediates.
- Complexation/inhibition without extra species measured: rational forms like -c0*A/(A + c1) can arise from quasi-steady binding/complex formation that reduces effective free A reactivity.
- Multiple pathways lumping: polynomial-in-A sums (c0 + c1*A + c2*A**2) often represent parallel reaction channels (e.g., zero-order initiation + first-order decay + autocatalytic route).

============================================================
GT Equivalence Verification (CRK18)
============================================================
GT: -c0*A**c1 + c2*_p*sin(c3*A)
Candidate formulas: 62

GT is a fixed function of **A only**:
\[
f(A)= -0.5637231318832533\,A^2 + 0.1313786441969526\,\sin(0.7616913890711074\,A).
\]
So any matching candidate must be reducible (by choosing its free constants) to **exactly** “quadratic in \(A\) + a single sine in \(A\)” with **no** linear term, constant offset, cosine term, logs/exp/sqrt/rational leftovers, absolute-value artifacts, or any \(t\)-dependence.

Below, for each candidate, I check whether we can zero out extra terms and tune remaining ones to match the two GT terms.

---

### 1
Has log, shifted square, cosine, linear, constant. Even if many coefficients set to 0, the log term is not a sine; cosine term can be removed. Remaining polynomial could match \(-0.5637A^2\) but cannot generate the sine term. **No**.

### 2
\[
A^2c0 + Ac1 + c2 + c3\cos(Ac4) + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)
\]
Set \(c1=0,c2=0,c3=0\). Then \(=c0A^2 + c5\sin(Ac6+c7)\). Choose \(c0=-0.5637231318832533\), \(c5=0.1313786441969526\), \(c6=0.7616913890711074\), \(c7=0\). Matches GT exactly. **Yes**.

### 3
Has cosine and log(exp(.)) term; can zero them, leaving \(A^2c0 + A(c1+c2)+c3\). Can match quadratic but cannot produce sine. **No**.

### 4
\[
A^2c0 + c1\sin(Ac2+c3)
\]
Choose \(c0=-0.5637231318832533\), \(c1=0.1313786441969526\), \(c2=0.7616913890711074\), \(c3=0\). Exact match. **Yes**.

### 5
Quadratic + linear + constants + cosine + logs. Logs cannot become sine for all \(A\). Even if logs/cos removed, no sine remains. **No**.

### 6
Linear terms + shifted square + cosine. No sine; cosine can’t become sine without phase but still cosine, and quadratic term is via \((A+c4)^2\) which introduces linear/constant unless forced; still no sine. **No**.

### 7
Has \(A^4 e^{A\cdot}\), exponentials, logs. Cannot reduce to just \(A^2\) + sine without leaving non-polynomial artifacts unless coefficients zeroed; then no sine. **No**.

### 8
Uses \(|A|^2\) (equals \(A^2\)) plus log(exp(.)) and log/A. No sine term available. **No**.

### 9
Quadratic + linear + constants + log(exp(.)) + log/A. No sine. **No**.

### 10
Quadratic + linear + rational term + cosine(log(.)) term. No sine; cosine(log(.)) cannot equal sine(linear) for all \(A\). **No**.

### 11
Quadratic + constant + cosine(affine). Could turn cosine into sine by phase shift, but cosine term would be \(\cos(Ac3+c4)\) and we need \(\sin(0.7616A)\) with **zero phase**. We could set \(c4=-\pi/2\) to get sine, yes. Then expression is \(A^2c0 + c1 + c2\sin(Ac3)\). Set \(c1=0\), \(c0=-0.5637\), \(c2=0.1313786\), \(c3=0.7616914\). Works. **Yes** (via cosine phase shift).

### 12
Quadratic + constant + sine. Set extra quadratic \(c1=0\), constant \(c2=0\); tune sine and quadratic. **Yes**.

### 13
Quadratic + constant + sine. Set constant \(c1=0\); tune. **Yes**.

### 14
Quadratic + constant + cosine. As in #11, cosine can be shifted to sine; set one quadratic coeff to 0 and constant to 0. **Yes**.

### 15
Constant + sine + \(|A|^2\) (i.e., \(A^2\)). Set constant \(c0=0\); tune \(c4=-0.5637\), sine amplitude/frequency/phase to match (phase 0). **Yes**.

### 16
Has \(|A|^3\), logs, log/A. Cannot become pure quadratic + sine unless those coefficients are 0; then left with linear+constant only. **No**.

### 17
Quadratic + \(A^{c1}\cos(\cdot)\) + constant + sine. You could zero the extra cosine term (set \(c2=0\)) and constant (set \(c5=0\)), leaving quadratic + sine. **Yes**.

### 18
Quadratic + linear + sine. Set linear \(c1=0\); tune quadratic and sine (phase 0). **Yes**.

### 19
Has \(t\) term and cosine. Must remove \(t\) dependence: set \(c2=0\). Then quadratic+linear+constant+cosine; no sine unless cosine phase-shifted and linear/constant removed. Set \(c1=0,c3=0\), and shift cosine to sine with \(c6=-\pi/2\). Then matches. **Yes**.

### 20
Has \(A^4 e^{A\cdot}\), rational, sqrt. Can’t reduce to quadratic+sine without killing those, leaving no sine. **No**.

### 21
Has linear, \(A\sin(\cdot)\) (note multiplied by A), shifted square, cosine. The \(A\sin(\cdot)\) cannot equal a pure \(\sin(kA)\) for all \(A\) unless coefficient 0, but then no sine. **No**.

### 22
Quadratic + linear + \(A^{c2}\) power + cosine + log. No sine; cosine could be shifted but then still extra power/log unless zeroed; then no sine. **No**.

### 23
Quadratic + constant + sine(A) + sine(t). Set \(c5=0\) to remove \(t\). Then same as #13: tune. **Yes**.

### 24
Has \( \exp(Ac6)\log(c7 t+1)\). To remove \(t\) for all \(t\), need \(c5=0\) (or impossible). Then reduces to quadratic+constant+sine(A). Tune constant to 0. **Yes**.

### 25
